# Story Bank

> Pipeline ý tưởng nội dung cho Afroyla.
> Mục tiêu: luôn có **15-20 items** across SEED + CONCEPT + READY.
> Cập nhật bởi `/idea-research` (thêm mới) và `/write-email` Phase 8 Kaizen (chuyển READY → USED).

---

## Pipeline Stages

| Stage | Ký hiệu | Định nghĩa | Tiêu chí chuyển lên |
|-------|---------|------------|---------------------|
| SEED | S- | Raw material: quote, Reddit find, news clip, personal anecdote | Có emotional potential (rated 3+/5) |
| CONCEPT | C- | Đã xác định Hook + Bridge + Product | Có thể nói throughline trong 1 câu |
| READY | R- | Outlined: opening scene, pivot, CTA, character, theme | Sẵn sàng hand off cho `/write-email` |
| USED | U- | Đã viết và gửi | Filed trong examples/, logged trong post-mortems |

---

## Inventory Summary

| Stage | Count | Target |
|-------|-------|--------|
| SEED | 141 | 10+ |
| CONCEPT | 22 | 5-8 |
| READY | 21 | 5-7 |
| **Total Active** | **184** | **15-20** |
| USED | 30 | — |

> **May 12 shipped:** U-030 "I bribed the photographer last night." (Pre-Order T-4 Color Reveal #2 + Customer-Chorus Cold-Open + 5-Beat CTA Architecture, MASS ~193K) — FREESTYLE (no R-ID) per user-directed scene (50-email customer flood after May 11 burgundy reveal + bribed-photographer overnight + 4 new colors back + tomorrow's price tease + SMS PRE opt-in CTA). 4 versions across 1 craft + 1 strategy + 1 brand review round (V1 → V2 craft PATCH 3-fix [burgundy image text-anchor placement per user push-back + CTA 5-beat restructure + naming-veto continuity fix] → V3 strategy GOOD-BUT-CAN-BE-STRONGER Direction A inversion to customer-chorus spine + 2 strategic tweaks [Guaranteed-first-text accuracy fix + May 13 forward-commitment lock] → V4 brand PASS WITH 2 PRE-PUBLISH DECISIONS Path A on P.S. trim + Path A on Renee name keep). **3 real customer voices used (raw verbatim per Rule #8 + #21):** C-0511i Anonymous YASSSSSS (peak-enthusiasm chorus opener line 2) + P-0511g Anonymous "feet" patient waiter (practical-feature middle) + G-0511a Renee (personality + named close + inline named-callback post-image per Terray May 1 precedent). **NEW BRAND PATTERNS documented (6 total):** (1) **Customer-chorus cold-open with hook-priority impact-led ordering** (NOT Rule #21 escalation) — 3 verbatim raw quotes ordered by visual impact, peak-enthusiasm first to stop scroll, then practical-feature, then personality+named close + Michelle narrator anchor line. Reusable for ANY post-broadcast-flood email where audience BEHAVIOR is the story. (2) **Inline named-callback after image reveal** — *"(Renee — the red is in there. You will be okay.)"* — Daniel-signature 1-line parenthetical nod to a named customer from cold-open after composite image lands. Mid-body intimacy without P.S. cost. (3) **5-beat CTA architecture (PRICE-TEASE → CAN-TELL → CANNOT-TELL → RISK → 3-STEP ACTION → REINFORCEMENT)** — replaces compound CTA that crammed instruction + action + benefit into one line. Numbered 3-step format scannable for mobile. (4) **"Updated tally" time-progression P.P.S.** — when body parenthetical mentions count (Keisha vetoed "one of mine") + P.P.S. wants to escalate (vetoed three), frame P.P.S. as "Updated tally." = time-progression gag between writing body + finishing email. Resolves continuity bug + adds comedic escalation. (5) **Photography team one-time-cameo P.S. trim** — when uncanonized character group introduced for single email's gag, P.S. should be trimmed to remove collective-voice attribution ("has asked me to clarify, on the record") → attribution-free version. Reduces canonization footprint per April 2026 Dylan/Jennifer reactive-canonization lesson. (6) **"Guaranteed first text" accurate CTA close** — when Pre-Order is open list (no gated seats per May 9 no-gate framing), SMS opt-in CTA close must accurately describe benefit: first-notification, NOT access. Replaces inaccurate "Guaranteed seat at the Pre-Order." **🔴 CRITICAL Forward Dependency:** *"Tomorrow. I promise."* + "What I cannot tell you today: the number." = brand-trust contract — May 13 BIG OFFER price-reveal email MUST ship per CD Tweak B lock. **Strategic watchouts post-ship:** 🔴 May 13 forward-commitment LOCKED (cannot slip) · 🟡 2-day plain-leather product-family thread (May 11 burgundy + May 12 four colors) — pivot product-family May 14-15 to avoid 4-day plain-leather fatigue · 🟡 Photography team canonization risk mitigated by P.S. trim but not eliminated — if reappears, run cast-bible spec session FIRST per April Dylan/Jennifer lesson · 🟡 Renee named-customer in MASS broadcast (193K) fits Terray May 1 precedent — watch reply pattern for policy validation · 🟡 P.P.S. naming-call expect inbox flood — CS team needs auto-ack + collect/route for May 13-15 content opportunity · 🟡 3rd consecutive email mentioning SMS PRE → 94923 (May 9 + May 11 doubled + May 12 numbered 3-step) — different framing each time mitigates fingerprint but watch opt-in conversion rate · 🟢 Female rebalance Day 14 preserved (Michelle solo body) · 🟢 Keisha rest preserved (action-only references) · 🟢 George rest after May 9-11 P.S. streak preserved · 🟢 Customer voices verbatim per Rule #8 + memory `feedback_customer_typos` (no callouts) · 🟢 Heritage value framing modern-only · 🟢 Em dash budget healthy (1/3 used) · 🟢 Memory compliance full pass (`feedback_no_fabrication` ✓ 3 real customer quotes user-supplied + user-directed bribe scene · `feedback_customer_typos` ✓ all emojis/caps/ellipses/exclamation stacks preserved · `feedback_writing_style` ✓ 5th-grade · `feedback_pivot_in_scene` ✓ · `feedback_no_corporate_character_intros` ✓ · `feedback_punchy_is_not_staccato` ✓ · `feedback_cold_reader_anchor_in_first_5_lines` ✓ · `feedback_no_grandmother_for_modern_collections` ✓ · `feedback_file_save_timing` ✓ saved post all 3 reviews). > **May 11 shipped:** U-029 "The maroon swatch came back." (Plain-Leather Pre-Order Photo Reveal + Feb 27 IWD-era Survey Arc Closure + SMS PRE Opt-in, MASS ~193K) — R-046 created May 11 via /idea-research same session + USED in single chain. 4 versions across 1 craft + 1 strategy + 1 brand review round (V1 → V2 craft PATCH 4-fix → V3 strategy GOOD-BUT-CAN-BE-STRONGER Direction B applied → V4 brand PASS WITH 2 PATCHES). **NEW BRAND PATTERNS documented (6 total):** (1) **Curiosity-ladder cold-open with explicit delayed-reveal mechanic** — Throssell-signature self-aware narrator move where Michelle explicitly tells reader *"I'm not going to show you what's inside yet"* + names the delay *"I want to tell you something first"* before pivoting to backstory. Image reveal becomes a payoff after ~75w of accumulated curiosity-debt. Reusable for ANY product-reveal email where Michelle has photo BEFORE reader. (2) **Multi-month dormant-thread arc closure** — when a prior survey/teaser email (Feb 27 IWD-era, 2.5 months dormant) reaches production-photo-arrives moment, callback to specific concrete details (9:14 PM Tuesday + Google Meet + maroon swatch) anchors loyal readers WITHOUT re-litigating full backstory. Compress to 30-35 words max. *"I argued. She won. You voted."* 3-beat payoff structure earns the short fragments via flowing 22-word setup. (3) **Two-product-family Pre-Order positioning via SCENE language NOT listicle** — when ONE Pre-Order contains TWO distinct product lines, explicit clarity required via scene language: *"The ones with words on the front and the ones without. Same hour. Same page. One Pre-Order, two ways to walk in."* Replaces V1's AI-fingerprint pattern (6-name parenthetical listicle + 4-fragment staccato closer). (4) **Doubled-up SMS CTA with VARIED framings** — when SMS opt-in is primary mechanic, mention 2x with DIFFERENT framings: early = "faster than waiting on your inbox to refresh" / closing = "takes two seconds, I'll text you before the email even queues." Different metaphors prevent repetition-fingerprint. (5) **Meta-acknowledgment reveal-line** — *"Okay. Here she is."* (4 words) preceding image = Throssell-pure self-aware narrator beat. Personification ("she" not "it") = luxury-fashion convention + community-voted-on warmth. (6) **George P.S. arc-closure callback with updated framing + new twist** — when callbacks to prior email P.S., update what's changed in-story (Feb 27: "did SHE go with black?" → May 11: "did the CUSTOMERS go with black?") + add new self-doubt beat at close ("Right?") = preserves loyal-reader payoff WITHOUT pure replay fatigue. **Strategic watchouts post-ship:** 🟡 First delayed-reveal cold-open in Afroyla MASS daily — watch reply signal "did the email break? I don't see the image" confusion + reader engagement metric time-to-scroll · 🟡 5-day Pre-Order thread (May 06→07→08→09→[10 MD pivot]→11) — fatigue mitigated via dormant-arc-revival product angle + cold-reader anchor · 🟡 Feb 27 IWD-era 2.5-month dormant-thread callback first-time in MASS — watch "I remember that email!" loyal-reader signal vs "what February call?" cold-reader confusion · 🟡 Two-product-family Pre-Order first-time — watch reader confusion ("which bags? same link?"), mitigated via explicit "same hour, same page, one Pre-Order, two ways to walk in" clarity · 🟡 SMS "PRE to 94923" doubled-up first time in single email — CS pre-brief required · 🟡 4-color reveal sequence opportunity (May 12-15) — V4 doesn't lock daily-by-daily, decision point for May 12 daily · 🟢 George P.S. callback with updated framing + "Right?" twist = arc-closure WITHOUT pure replay fatigue (brand-critic flag mitigated) · 🟢 Keisha rest preserved (action cameo only, dormant-arc-revival = fresh role per May 09 watchout) · 🟢 Female rebalance Day 13 preserved · 🟢 Customer voices verbatim per Rule #8 + memory `feedback_customer_typos` NO callouts (Syretta "like" grammar marker preserved post brand-critic V3→V4 patch) · 🟢 Heritage value framing modern-reclamation per `feedback_no_grandmother_for_modern_collections` · 🟢 Cold-reader anchor by line 5 · 🟢 Memory compliance full pass (`feedback_no_fabrication` ✓ Feb 27 + 3 customer voices + pricing/ship hedged · `feedback_customer_typos` ✓ Syretta "like" preserved no callout · `feedback_writing_style` ✓ 5th-grade · `feedback_pivot_in_scene` ✓ image inside narrated reveal · `feedback_no_corporate_character_intros` ✓ Keisha/customers/George via action+name only · `feedback_punchy_is_not_staccato` ✓ all short beats earned by flowing setup · `feedback_cold_reader_anchor_in_first_5_lines` ✓ · `feedback_no_grandmother_for_modern_collections` ✓ · `feedback_file_save_timing` ✓ inline only until SHIP). > **May 10 shipped:** U-028 "Happy Mother's Day." — pure-Michelle greeting card + soft store P.S. (MASS ~193K, MD day-of). R-045 created May 10 via /idea-research same session + USED in single chain. **First daily of cycle without commercial body** — Hot Dog = meta-acknowledgment ("That's the email. That's the whole thing."), Broccoli = WIDENING DEFINITION of motherhood (not bio-moms-only) as the brand value delivered, not a product. 3 versions across 1 craft review round + 2 user direction redirects (layout re-flow per "viết dính chùm hết với nhau bị khó đọc" + soft store P.S. add). **NEW BRAND PATTERNS documented:** (1) **Greeting card format departure as deliberate brand choice** — cultural anchor day with enough emotional weight = the greeting can BE the email. Pre-document waivers in Story Bank READY entry (Rule #2 Michelle IN scene → direct-address interpretation, Rule #4 TURN → implicit, Rule #22 product-in-scene → waived in body, Rule #23 P.S. connected → required) so /review-craft applies standards with format awareness, no false-positive flags. (2) **Anti-marketing meta-line opener for greeting/holiday emails** — lead with the literal greeting then immediately self-aware acknowledge the bare-minimum framing ("That's the email. That's the whole thing — except I want to say it wider"). Throssell-Settle reader-trust play. Earns trust to do MORE in body. (3) **Widening list with sentence-length variation breaks Rule #28 echo-writing** — "And to..." / "To the [X] who [Y]" cadence borderline mitigated by (a) sentence-length variation within each cluster, (b) standalone short paragraphs breaking pattern (the 2 AM friend + "To her especially" fragment), (c) different opener verbs per paragraph. Reusable for inclusive-list / honor-roll emails. (4) **Grief beat 1-paragraph 3-sentence dose with paired em-dash pause + grounded metaphor** — "If you're carrying today alone — because mom passed... at all — today is still your day. The grief and the day are not enemies. They sit on the couch together." 1-beat MAX NOT sermon (per R-038 watchout). Couch metaphor grounds abstract. Anything longer = sermon, anything shorter = dismissive. (5) **Anti-urgency soft store P.S. preserves gratitude tone** — when adding commercial element mid-finalize, default to anti-urgency framing (no %off / countdown / code / "ends tonight"). Visible link enough. "The one your eye keeps going back to is usually the right one" = customer self-selection cue, brand "the prize" stance. (6) **Format type drives layout choices, not just sentence-level rules** — greeting card ≠ daily story = different paragraph density target. Whitespace = typographic element, standalone beats earn emotional weight by what surrounds them. **Strategic watchouts post-ship:** 🟡 First "no-product email" precedent in MASS daily — watch reply signal (engagement-only metric, no conversion path) · 🟡 CS team brief required: expect "thank you" replies + emotional "I just lost my mom this year" replies → Tasha/Jennifer pre-brief for emotional-reply routing template · 🟡 Keisha post-arc rest Day 1 (5-day fatigue from U-024→U-027) — May 11+ Keisha can return BUT not as collection-thread continuation; fresh role required if reintroduced · 🟡 W19 Day 8 closes → W20 starts May 11 — recommend `/weekly-planning` session before May 11 daily · 🟡 Pre-Order weekend May 16-17 production prep timeline — confirm with team before May 13 · 🟢 Female rebalance Day 12 preserved (Michelle solo direct-address + universal-women audience — no team cameos, no customer voice per user direction "pure Michelle") · 🟢 Heritage anchor R-033 Emma Clarissa Clement still READY for any future MD-adjacent slot (was originally pre-LOCKED for May 9, displaced by U-027, now available for next heritage-anchor opportunity) · 🟢 Subject↔preview asymmetry pattern reuse from U-027 (subject = literal greeting, preview = curiosity gap) · 🟢 Memory compliance full pass (`feedback_no_fabrication` ✓ no invented details · `feedback_writing_style` ✓ văn nói 5th-grade · `feedback_no_corporate_character_intros` ✓ Michelle solo · `feedback_punchy_is_not_staccato` ✓ short paragraphs earned by flowing setup · `feedback_cold_reader_anchor_in_first_5_lines` ✓ WHO/WHAT/STAKE by line 3 · `feedback_file_save_timing` ✓ saved post /finalize-email). Bank: 183 active.

> **May 09 shipped:** U-027 "Five Hundred Yeses" — "I needed 100. You sent almost 500." (Pre-Order Resolution + soft Amazon Closure, MASS ~193K) — R-044 created May 09 via /idea-research same session + USED in single chain. Arc resolution: 4-day Keisha collection thread (U-024 → U-025 → U-026 → U-027). 6 versions across 1 craft review round + 1 strategy review round (brand SKIPPED). **NEW BRAND PATTERNS documented:** (1) **Customer-chorus opener with conditional Y voices** — 2 verbatim Pre-Order Y replies (H F C-0508d + Caralen C-0508f) framed inside flowing setup ("A few from this morning alone:") + flowing bridge ("They haven't stopped"). Per Rule #21 escalating order: enthusiasm → comedy/practical. Conditional caveats ("YES…… I have my favorites, but I can't order any just yet" + "I would say Y. But I have to see the price first....lol") ENRICH celebration vs dilute — readers recognize budget-honest reality, social proof lands HARDER with caveats than with clean cheerleader voices. **Reusable for any community-vote celebration email — actively seek conditional voices over pure cheerleader voices.** (2) **No-gate Pre-Order positioning** — when community-trigger Pre-Order opens to whole list (not voter-only gated), close with "You didn't earn a head start. You earned the [thing] itself" pattern. Inverts marketing default of gating-as-reward → reframes participation-as-reward. Honors voters' impact without creating exclusion. **Reusable across any community-trigger mechanic that opens to mass list.** (3) **Re-stacked channel-sunset P.P.S. logic** — when business intent involves channel migration/wind-down, NEVER mix migration message with cross-channel CTA. V3 had 3-signal chaos (sale-ends-on-Amazon + Amazon-closing + go-to-afroyla.com = 3 different routes in 50 words). V4 re-stacked: ONE destination (Amazon) + TWO urgency layers (price increase + channel sunset). Wind-down framing flipped from contradiction to urgency-amplifier ("after Sunday prices go up + after a few weeks the door closes entirely = today is the cleanest window if Amazon is your channel"). **Reusable: pick the channel + stack urgency reasons + state in escalating order.** (4) **Action-led reaction cold-open as Rule #36 alternative** — when prior emails used direct-address recap ("Yesterday's email...") or narrative-context-block ("Earlier this week, I asked you..."), switch to action-led reaction ("I just sat back from the inbox and I'm still laughing") to avoid template-repeat fingerprint. Implicit-LOL via "still laughing" preserves user-voice energy without dropping into SMS register. (5) **Image asset reuse for arc-closure (Rule #18 nuance)** — for arc-closure emails 1-2 days from product reveal, reusing reveal image creates visual-thread payoff for warm readers + visual anchor for cold readers (who treat fresh). Rule #18 doesn't apply because not "borrowed details across separate emails" — it's continuity within sealed arc. (6) **Subject↔preview asymmetry** — subject = data/anomaly hook ("I needed 100. You sent almost 500."), preview = character/comedy hook ("And Keisha went quiet for ten minutes. Then she texted 'okay.'"). Two different angles, complementary, neither repeats. **Lesson learned (caught in review):** business-routing intent (which channel, which link) MUST be verified BEFORE drafting CTA — don't assume from narrative framing. V3 routed to afroyla.com from "consolidation" narrative assumption; user direction during /review-craft flagged this as fact-flaw not craft choice. **Strategic watchouts post-ship:** 🟡 4-day Keisha-arc complete (U-024→U-025→U-026→U-027) — May 10 (tomorrow, Mother's Day) MUST pivot away from Keisha thread (5 days = fatigue). Heritage anchor candidates: R-033 Emma Clarissa Clement (pre-LOCKED for May 9 originally — could move to May 10) OR R-035 Caralen Ripple OR R-038 Theresa Bereaved MD redirect · 🟡 No-gate Pre-Order positioning = first-time pattern — watch for reader reply confusion ("am I in the Pre-Order? do I need to do anything?") + CS pre-brief required to handle "I replied Y, what now?" inquiries with "you'll get the link next weekend with everyone else, no separate gating" template · 🟡 Amazon channel-sunset soft signal = first explicit foreshadow in MASS daily — watch for reply signal "are you really closing Amazon? when?" + leadership decision needed for follow-up email confirmation/denial · 🟡 Pre-Order weekend May 16-17 production prep + payment link readiness — confirm with team before May 13 · 🟡 H F + Caralen voices consumed (chorus opener) — Caralen identifier collision with S-0501a Deaconess Caralen (different person) — distinguish as "Pre-Order Caralen" if cited again · 🟢 Arc-resolution clean (4-day thread closes without dangling threads) · 🟢 Female rebalance Day 11 preserved (Michelle solo body + Keisha off-stage texting only) · 🟢 Joy-led palate cleanser after 4 consecutive heavy/operational emails · 🟢 Cold-reader anchor preserved despite chorus-opener structure (context lands by line 5) · 🟢 Memory compliance full pass (`feedback_no_fabrication` — both Y voices REAL + soft Amazon language; `feedback_customer_typos` — "YES……" 6-dot + "....lol" 4-dot lowercase preserved with NO callouts; `feedback_writing_style` văn nói 5th-grade; `feedback_pivot_in_scene`; `feedback_no_corporate_character_intros`; `feedback_punchy_is_not_staccato`; `feedback_cold_reader_anchor_in_first_5_lines`; `feedback_no_grandmother_for_modern_collections`; `feedback_file_save_timing` saved post /finalize-email). Bank: 183 active.

### R-045-archived: "Happy Mother's Day." — Pure-Michelle Greeting Card (MASS, May 10 day-of)
- **Theme:** Cultural Moment (Mother's Day day-of) + Michelle's World (direct-address gratitude letter)
- **Story Source:** Cultural Moment (Mother's Day) + Behind the Scenes (Michelle's day-of reflection)
- **Emotional Driver:** Gratitude → Inclusion → Quiet warmth
- **Campaign Job:** None — Daily (W19 Sunday May 10, MD day-of)
- **Format DEPARTURE from infotainment template:** This is a GREETING CARD, not an infotainment story email. Per user direction May 10: "tôi chỉ muốn gửi 1 email chúc mừng Happy Mother's Day cho các khách hàng của Afroyla thôi" + "pure Michelle" voice. NO customer voices. NO product push. NO CTA. NO story arc. Style Rule #1 (one throughline) preserved; Rule #2 (Michelle in scene) interpreted as Michelle DIRECT-ADDRESS rather than narrating a scene. Rule #3 (inhabit) softened — this is a card, not a scene.
- **Hook (Hot Dog):**
  > "Happy Mother's Day."
  >
  > That's the email. That's the whole thing.
  >
  > But I want to say it wider than a card aisle.
- **Bridge (3-beat — short, warm, direct):**
  1. **The opener (no setup, no story):** "Happy Mother's Day." Plain. No clever cold open. Just the words first. Then 1-2 lines acknowledging that's the whole point of the email — Michelle isn't selling anything today, isn't pitching anything, just saying it.
  2. **The widening (the throughline):** Today belongs wider than the card aisle makes it look. Name them: biological mothers. Godmothers. Aunts who raised you when nobody else did. Older cousins who became mothers without title. The friend who showed up at 2 AM the year your world fell apart. Stepmothers. Grandmothers raising grandchildren. Women who chose not to have kids and poured into other people's anyway. Women who mother themselves because nobody else did. AND — softly — the women carrying today alone, because mom passed, or mom doesn't speak to them, or never spoke to them at all. Today's still their day too.
  3. **The Michelle close (gratitude, brief):** 2-3 lines. Something like — "Whatever shape your today takes, I'm grateful you let me into your inbox while it's happening. That's not a small thing. Happy Mother's Day, [first name]." Sign-off: "Love, Michelle."
- **Optional P.S. (1 line max — Michelle voice):** "If you're carrying today alone, I see you. Today's still your day." OR omit entirely for cleanest card. ⚠️ DO NOT add Amazon CTA, sale acknowledgment, or any commercial line — would dilute gratitude tone. Yesterday's U-027 P.P.S. already handled Amazon last-call.
- **Product (Broccoli):** NONE. This is a no-product email. The "broccoli" is the WIDER MOTHER'S DAY DEFINITION (the inclusion frame is the brand value, not the bag).
- **Character:** Michelle solo POV, direct-address letter format · NO team cameos (female rebalance Day 12 preserved — Michelle alone) · NO customer voices (per user direction "pure Michelle") · NO Keisha (5-day fatigue rest from arc U-024→U-027)
- **Throughline:** Today belongs wider than the card aisle makes it look. To every woman who poured into someone — you are who today is for.
- **Subject Line Ideas:**
  - "Happy Mother's Day."
  - "Happy Mother's Day, [first name]."
  - "Today is the day."
  - "Wider than the card aisle."
  - "For every woman who poured into someone."
- **Preview Line Ideas:**
  - "That's the whole email. But I want to say it wider."
  - "Including the women not in the card aisle."
  - "Including the ones carrying today alone."
- **Structure:** Direct opener ("Happy Mother's Day.") → Michelle voice acknowledgment that this is the whole email → widening list (4-7 categories of mother-figures, including grief beat) → Michelle gratitude close (2-3 lines) → sign-off "Love, Michelle" → optional 1-line P.S.
- **Law check:**
  - #1 ONE throughline ✓ (today is wider than the card aisle)
  - #2 Michelle IN scene — INTERPRETED as direct-address letter (not scene-based; greeting card format)
  - #3 Inhabit — SOFTENED (greeting card, not scene)
  - #5 Don't pre-sell ✓ (no sale)
  - #6 Standalone ✓
  - #8 Customer voices ✓ — N/A per user direction (pure Michelle)
  - #17 Em dash ≤ 2-3 ✓ (target — likely 1-2 in widening list)
  - #21 Real customer voices ✓ — N/A
  - #22 Product in scene ✓ — N/A (no product)
  - #26 No naked pivot ✓ (no pivot needed — single-throughline letter)
  - #36 No self-template repeat ✓ (direct "Happy Mother's Day" opener differs from May 06-09 sequence: May 06 declarative confession / May 07 direct-address recap / May 08 narrative-context-block / May 09 action-led inbox reaction)
  - #38 No meta-narration — "That's the email" borderline self-aware but lands as Michelle voice signature, not labeling-the-bit. Acceptable.
- **⚠️ Risks / Watchouts:**
  - 🔴 **Format departure from daily template** — readers expect Afroyla daily story. Greeting card may feel "thin" without the usual narrative meat. Mitigation: Michelle's brand voice + the widening list does the emotional work; the THINNESS IS THE POINT (a real card is short).
  - 🟡 **No-CTA email** — first daily of the cycle without ANY conversion path. Watch open/reply rates as engagement-only signal.
  - 🟡 **Grief beat (women carrying alone)** — must stay 1-line restrained, NOT sermon. Reference R-038 watchout: "1-beat MAX, NOT essay." Per memory `feedback_writing_style` — văn nói, không triết lý nhiều tầng.
  - 🟡 **List rhythm in widening section** — 4-7 categories listed sequentially risks staccato per memory `feedback_punchy_is_not_staccato`. Mitigation: vary sentence length within list, use connective tissue ("and", "or", "and the woman who"), avoid 4+ identical-structure short lines back-to-back.
  - 🟡 **Subject line vs body** — "Happy Mother's Day" subject IS the body opener. Risk: redundant. Mitigation: subject can stay literal ("Happy Mother's Day."), preview line carries the curiosity gap ("That's the whole email. But I want to say it wider.").
  - 🟡 **Pivot from Keisha thread (Day 12 since arc start)** — confirmed clean (no Keisha mention, no Pre-Order callback in body, no Amazon last-call). U-027 yesterday closed the arc; today opens fresh.
  - 🟢 **Female rebalance Day 12 preserved** ✓ (Michelle solo + universal-women audience)
  - 🟢 **Heritage value implicit** ✓ (Black mother lineage explicit in audience framing — Afroyla audience IS Black women, the "wider than the card aisle" inclusion lands inside that frame without forced anchor)
  - 🟢 **Boldness in restraint** ✓ — sending a no-product, no-CTA email on the calendar's biggest gift day = brand "the prize" stance
  - 🟢 **Memory compliance:** `feedback_no_fabrication` ✓ (no invented details), `feedback_writing_style` ✓ (5th-grade văn nói, skim-friendly), `feedback_no_corporate_character_intros` ✓ (Michelle solo, no team), `feedback_punchy_is_not_staccato` ✓ (mitigation in list rhythm watchout), `feedback_cold_reader_anchor_in_first_5_lines` ✓ ("Happy Mother's Day" + "That's the email" delivers WHO/WHAT/STAKE in line 1-3)
- **Source:** User direction May 10 ("tôi chỉ muốn gửi 1 email chúc mừng Happy Mother's Day cho các khách hàng của Afroyla thôi" + "pure Michelle") + cultural calendar (May 10 2026 = Mother's Day, US) + arc-pivot requirement from U-027 May 09 P.P.S. ("MUST pivot away from Keisha thread")
- **Added:** 2026-05-10
- **🔒 LOCKED for May 10 daily slot. Hand off to `/write-email`.**
- **Pre-flight requirements (CONFIRM before `/write-email`):** (1) Length target = 200-300 words (greeting card scope, NOT 500-600 daily standard) · (2) NO product, NO CTA, NO Amazon mention · (3) Sign-off = "Love, Michelle." · (4) Optional 1-line P.S. for grief beat (Option 2 in proposal) — user to confirm include/omit · (5) Subject = literal "Happy Mother's Day." or "Happy Mother's Day, [first name]." — preview line carries curiosity gap

  > I know that sounds blunt. I'm being blunt because Mona Haynes wrote me yesterday and said the quiet part out loud:
  >
  > *"As a procrastinating human, it took me a while to actually place an order. I had started many orders but never completed them but this time I completed the order."*
- **Bridge (story → product, in scene) — 8-beat structure:**
  1. **Stakes-first declaration cold open** (NEW mechanic) — urgency in line 1, attribution to Mona in line 3
  2. **Mona verbatim opener** (subject↔body callback at paragraph 3)
  3. **3-question verbatim burst** (when bags arrive + 90-yr-old purple selection + previously ordered purses with 4 exclamation marks — typos preserved, no callouts)
  4. **Recognition beat** ("I knew that woman. I have BEEN that woman. The cart that opens and closes in your browser. The tab you keep meaning to come back to.")
  5. **TURN-as-synthesis** ("Mona asked three questions. But really, she's asking one: *did I click in time?*")
  6. **Continuity callback to U-022 mid-body** (NOT cold open) — "Yesterday I wrote about the Amazon door that just opened... That door is still open today."
  7. **Buffer-not-wall beat** — airport-countdown simile + 11 PM tissue-paper inhabit + "It's not a wall. Just a buffer. The buffer just keeps shrinking."
  8. **Imani gift-suggestion answer + inline product image + Sunday-morning sit-still beat + Imani-as-example reframe** ("The Imani is one bag. There are sixteen others on the Amazon page right now. Mona's lady might want a different one. Yours might too.")
  9. **Price story** ($45.54 from $142.95 — math only, no percentage spelled out per /review-strategy Cut C2)
  10. **CTA + close** — Amazon storefront button (continuation of U-022) + "Mona clicked. The 90-year-old who loves purple doesn't know it yet, but Sunday is coming for her too."
  11. **P.S.** — Mona service-recovery acknowledgment + Jennifer-from-Support 1:1 reply deferral + Imani gift-pick close ("Hope Sunday lands on time for both of you")
- **Product (Broccoli):** Imani Afrocentric Art HandBag (example) — $45.54 today / $142.95 normal (68% off) on Amazon. Plus open-line CTA "Bags from $39.95 · Up to 68% OFF · Prime Free Shipping · Arrives 4 days before Mother's Day."
- **Character:** Michelle solo POV + Mona Haynes verbatim cascade + 90-yr-old purple-lover off-stage + Jennifer P.S. 1-line operational mention. NO George/Keisha/Marcus/Tasha/Alice/Nia. Female rebalance day 7.
- **Throughline:** "Mona finally clicked. Then asked: did I click in time? + can you help me pick the next one for a 90-year-old purple-lover? — She's asking the question every late-clicker is feeling. Today, here's the answer."
- **Subject Line (SHIPPED):** "As a procrastinating human..."
- **Preview Line (SHIPPED):** "Today is the day to be done with that."

### R-026-archived: "Solomon Called Me Sister. Then Elias. Then Ben." — Men's Line Survey (Father's Day Validation)
- **Theme:** Industry Commentary + Community Co-creation + Customer Voice (men's voices triangulated)

  >
  > Maybe. That's why I'm writing you.
- **Bridge (story → survey, in scene) — SIMPLIFIED 6-beat structure:**
  1. **The announcement** (cold open) — "Afroyla is going to make something for men. Maybe. That's why I'm writing you."
  2. **The why — male customers asking (3 voices, lighter touch than essay version):** "For months now, men have been showing up. Buying for their wives. Their mothers. Their sisters.   3. **George cameo (the husband angle — light, opinionated, sitcom-tone):** "And George. George has OPINIONS. George has been giving me opinions every time I open the laptop. George has thoughts about wallets. About straps. About 'where the phone goes, Michelle.' George is convinced he should be on the design team. Keisha disagrees."
  4. **Father's Day target + Keisha's status (honest, not over-promising):** "We're trying to make this happen for Father's Day. June 21. Eight weeks. Keisha has been sketching. She has a few ideas. Honestly — we're not WOW'd yet. Some are close. Some are not. We don't want to ship 'fine.' We want to ship something men actually want to carry."
  5. **The audience question (the ask):** "So I'm coming to you first. The ones who'd actually buy this for him. Your husband. Your son. Your boyfriend. Your dad. Your brother. Would you? And if yes — what does HE need? What would make him say yes?"
  6. **CTA + button — survey:** Three minutes. Rate what we have. Tell us what's missing. → `Take the 3-min survey →`

  8. **P.S.** — George angle: "George wants me to mention that he's available for product testing. I told him product testing is not a paid position. He said 'depends on the product, Michelle.'"

### R-025-archived: "Some Of Us Picked The Career." — Different Math, Same Mother's Day
- **Theme:** Industry Commentary (zoomed out — phenomenon, not person) + Michelle's World + soft MD-shipping pivot
- **Story Source:** Industry Commentary (cultural moment around Black women prioritizing career over family) + Michelle reflection
- **Emotional Driver:** Curiosity → Honest Reflection → Belonging (cả hai phía đều là phụ nữ Black, đều có giá trị)
- **Campaign Job:** None — Daily (W18 Mon, soft MD-deadline reminder)
- **Throughline:** Một số chị em chúng ta chọn sự nghiệp. Một số chọn gia đình. Cả hai đều phải trả giá. Cả hai đều xứng đáng được tôn vinh ngày Chủ Nhật thứ hai của tháng Năm.
- **Hook (Hot Dog):**
  > Có một cuộc trò chuyện đang diễn ra trên mạng tuần này.
  >
  > Về một người phụ nữ Black thành đạt nói thẳng rằng tuần nào cô ấy cũng chỉ dành tối đa 3 tiếng cuối tuần cho con.
  >
  > Mọi người tranh cãi.
  >
  > Tôi đọc xong, đóng laptop, ngồi đó một lúc.
- **Bridge (story → product → MD pivot, in scene):**
  1. **Setup không gọi tên:** Michelle không nêu tên. Không link. "Bạn có thể đã thấy hoặc không. Không quan trọng cô ấy là ai. Quan trọng là — đây không phải câu chuyện của một người. Đây là câu chuyện của rất nhiều chị em chúng ta."
  2. **Acknowledge cái nhóm phụ nữ này có thật:** "Một số chị em chúng ta chọn sự nghiệp. Đặt nó lên đầu. Cố ý. Không xin lỗi. Xây công ty. Leo C-suite. Mở phòng khám. Mở studio. Có con — và quyết định sẽ không là người mẹ ngồi bên giường mỗi tối kể chuyện cổ tích. Đó là lựa chọn. Lựa chọn thật. Họ biết mình đang chọn gì."
  3. **Acknowledge cái giá — không lên án:** "Có một cái giá. Lúc nào cũng có. Đứa con sẽ nhớ ai đón nó ở trường mẫu giáo. Ai pha cốc sữa lúc 2 giờ sáng. Ai cười khi nó bước vào phòng. Đôi khi đó là mẹ. Đôi khi đó là bà ngoại. Đôi khi đó là cô. Đôi khi đó là người trông trẻ. Đứa con sẽ biết. Sớm hay muộn. Nó sẽ biết."
  4. **Cái nguyên tắc (user's frame — life is tradeoffs):** "Cuộc đời là sự lựa chọn và đánh đổi. Không thể toàn vẹn được mọi thứ. Bạn ưu tiên thứ gì hơn — bạn sẽ dành nhiều sự quan tâm, thời gian cho điều đó. Cái còn lại sẽ ít đi. Đó là toán học. Không phải đạo đức."
  5. **The TURN — không có phía nào sai:** "Người chị em chọn sự nghiệp — chị ấy không sai. Chị ấy đang xây một thứ rồi sẽ thuê hàng trăm phụ nữ Black khác. Đang chứng minh chúng ta có thể ngồi vào bàn đó. Người chị em chọn ở nhà với con, với bà, với gia đình — chị ấy cũng không sai. Chị ấy đang giữ một thứ mà nếu không có chị ấy giữ thì không ai giữ. Cả hai đều đang gánh một phần khác nhau của cùng một mái nhà."
  6. **Beat ngắn cho người đọc thật của Michelle (KHÔNG name-drop ai):** "Tôi viết email này mỗi sáng cho một danh sách. Phần lớn các chị trong danh sách này — không có lựa chọn 3 tiếng. Đi làm 8 tiếng. Về nhà nấu cơm. Đưa đón con. Chăm mẹ. Đi nhà thờ Chủ Nhật. Đó là toán của các chị. Không phải vì các chị thích nó. Vì đó là cách các chị giữ mọi thứ đứng vững."
  7. **Pivot (in scene — body action, NOT naked pivot):** "Tôi nghĩ về tất cả những điều này, rồi nhìn lên lịch trên tường. Mother's Day là Chủ Nhật, ngày 10 tháng 5. Hai tuần nữa. Dù chị là người chọn sự nghiệp, hay người chọn gia đình, hay người không có lựa chọn — Chủ Nhật đó là ngày của chị. Hoặc là ngày của người đã giúp chị trở thành chị."
  8. **Soft CTA (in scene):** "Nếu chị đang nghĩ đến việc tặng một người trong tháng này — đợt giảm giá Mother's Day vẫn đang chạy đến hết ngày 10/5, lên tới 60% off. Để kịp tay người ấy vào sáng Mother's Day, đặt trước ngày 1/5. Đó là deadline lịch tự đặt ra, không phải tôi đặt ra."
  9. **Button:** `Get 60% OFF Deal →`
  10. **Close (humble, không moralize):** "Không có phía nào trong cuộc trò chuyện tuần này là sai. Chỉ là toán khác nhau. Chủ Nhật ngày 10 — chúng ta cùng tôn vinh tất cả các phép toán."
- **Product (Broccoli):** Heritage Tote OR Imarimom Small Leather Handbag — gợi tên 1 bag duy nhất trong scene, không listicle. 60% OFF + May 1 cutoff lồng vào body action ("nhìn lên lịch") — KHÔNG corporate block. Không nói "for the mom who chose career" hay "for the mom who chose family" — để người đọc tự nhận.
- **Character:**
  - **Michelle** solo POV — đọc, ngồi xuống, suy nghĩ, nhìn lịch, viết
  - ⚠️ **KHÔNG gọi tên** Emma Grede / SKIMS / WSJ
  - ⚠️ **KHÔNG gọi tên** Coretta / Toni Morrison / Maya Angelou (đối xứng — nếu Michelle không gọi tên Emma, cũng không vũ trang ai để chống lại Emma)
  - ⚠️ **NO team cameo** (Keisha/Marcus/Tasha/Alice/Nia OFF — Michelle solo reflection email)
  - **George P.S.** — skip hoặc 1 dòng nhẹ ngoài chủ đề (anh ấy đã xuất hiện Apr 24 + 26)
- **Law check:**
  - #1 ONE throughline ✓ (different math, both valid, both honored on May 10)
  - #2 Michelle IN scene ✓ (đọc, đóng laptop, ngồi, nhìn lịch)
  - #3 Inhabit ✓ (cuộc trò chuyện trên mạng, cái laptop đóng lại, cái lịch trên tường)
  - #4 Turn ✓ (đọc xong tưởng sẽ phán xét → sit with it → reframe thành "different math")
  - #5 Don't pre-sell ✓ (jump-cut vào, không "let me tell you about a debate...")
  - #6 Standalone ✓ (không cần đọc tin tức để hiểu — Michelle setup phenomenon)
  - #8 Opening = phenomenon + Michelle's body action trong 4-5 lines ✓
  - #9 Product stays in scene ✓ (calendar pivot via body action — Rule #26 ✓)
  - #17 Em dash ≤ 2-3 ✓ (target)
  - #22 Product in scene ✓
  - #28 No echo writing ✓ (vary "Một số chị em..." structure across paragraphs)
- **Subject Line Ideas:**
  - "Some of us picked the career."
  - "There's a conversation happening this week."
  - "Two kinds of mothers. Same Sunday."
  - "I closed my laptop and sat with this."
  - "Different math. Same Mother's Day."
- **Structure:**
  1. Cold open — phenomenon framing + Michelle's body action (closed laptop, sat with it)
  2. Setup không gọi tên (whoever she is doesn't matter — story is about MANY of us)
  3. Acknowledge career-prioritizing women exist (NOT wrong, intentional choice, no apology)
  4. Acknowledge the cost (kid will know who showed up — fact, not guilt)
  5. The principle (life is tradeoffs — math, not morality)
  6. The TURN (both kinds of mothers carrying different parts of the same house)
  7. Beat for Michelle's actual readers (the "no choice" women holding everything up)
  8. Pivot via calendar glance (May 10, two weeks)
  9. Soft CTA + button (60% OFF, May 1 cutoff)
  10. Close — neither side is wrong, just different math
- **Campaign Fit:** Apr 27 W18 Day 1 daily — opens the post-MD-sale recovery week with a non-sales philosophy beat that earns the soft 60% OFF nudge. Bridges from R-024 (Reggie male-gifter) → R-025 (career-choosing women) → both end with same May 10 calendar math. Establishes W18 as "honoring the math" theme.
- **⚠️ Watchouts:**
  - DO NOT name Emma Grede / SKIMS / WSJ. "Một người phụ nữ Black thành đạt" là đủ. Ai biết thì biết — ai không biết, không ảnh hưởng đến hiểu email.
  - DO NOT vũ khí hóa Toni Morrison / Coretta / Maya Angelou để chống lại Emma. Đối xứng: nếu Emma không xuất hiện, đối thủ của Emma cũng không xuất hiện.
  - DO NOT dùng từ "controversy" / "backlash" / "calling out" / "drama". Đây là "một cuộc trò chuyện" — soft framing.
  - DO NOT so sánh "career mom" vs "stay-at-home mom" thành kèo win-lose.
  - DO NOT biến cái "đứa con sẽ nhớ" beat (#3) thành đe dọa các bà mẹ sự nghiệp. Frame là FACT, không phải GUILT. "Sớm hay muộn nó sẽ biết" — không thêm phán xét. Chỉ là true.
  - 60% OFF + May 1 phải nằm INSIDE Michelle's body action ("nhìn lên lịch") — không corporate P.S.
  - Verify 60% OFF khớp với MD pricing thực tế trên site trước khi gửi.
  - Verify May 1 cutoff khớp với Marcus's shipping math.
  - Per memory rule `feedback_writing_style.md` — Grade-5 vocabulary, văn nói, skim-friendly. Avoid triết lý nhiều tầng.

### R-024-archived: "Signed: Grandfather With 11 Females I Love The Mostest" — Reggie Wrote Me Back
- **Theme:** Customer Voice + Family/Personal + soft MD-shipping-deadline pivot
- **Story Source:** Customer Voice (rare male-gifter voice + post-Survey reply continuity from U-014 Apr 24)
- **Emotional Driver:** Pride + Vulnerability→Strength + tender humor → soft MD urgency
- **Campaign Job:** None — Daily (post-sale palate cleanser with light deadline reminder)
- **Hook (Hot Dog):** Reggie wrote me back. Replying to the email Keisha and I were fighting over. He didn't pick a backpack. He told me about the day he gave his wife the bag. The surprise. Her face. The moment that made him "extremely proud." Then he signed off the email like this:
  > *"Signed by a grandfather with 11 females in my family i love the mostest."*
  
  I read that last line three times.
- **Bridge (story → product → MD pivot, in scene):**
  1. **The reply lands** — Apr 24 Survey went to MASS asking which 3 of 6 backpacks. Most replies were women voting. Reggie's was about a purse he'd already bought. Wrong question, right answer.
  2. **The wife's face beat (verbatim block — DO NOT trim):**
     > *"The purse and handbag that I have received so far were in perfect condition and made very nice gifts. I was extremely proud when I saw my wife's face as it was a surprise... Signed by a grandfather with 11 females in my family i love the mostest."*
     
     ⚠️ Quote ends here. **DO NOT include Reggie's USPS/shipping concern paragraph** (per user direction Apr 26 — strip it from quote).
  3. **The math** — 11 women. One grandfather. The arithmetic of love most men never put on paper. Michelle doesn't list the 11 — Reggie didn't either. Just the number. Just "the mostest."
  4. **"The mostest"** — that word. The way you reach for it when "most" doesn't carry the weight. Michelle realizes: Reggie wasn't writing a love letter. The love letter snuck in.
  5. **Pivot (smooth, in scene — NOT a corporate block):** Reggie's wife has the Kadia. The Eliora — also Top Grain Leather — is in transit. He's working through the 11. Which means he ordered before today. Which is good. Because Mother's Day is May 10 — that's two weeks. The Early MD Sale closed Thursday but the broader MD pricing (up to **60% OFF**) runs until May 10. The catch: if you want it in her hands BEFORE May 10, **order by May 1.** That gives our shipping the runway it needs. Not a deadline I'm inventing. A deadline the calendar invented.
  6. **Address to reader (warm, no hard sell):** If you're a grandfather working through your own list — Reggie is two ahead of you. If you're a daughter or a son or a husband who's been meaning to — May 1 is the cutoff for "before May 10." After that, we'll still ship, but I can't promise the morning.
  7. **Soft close:** No CTA button mandatory. Maybe one inline link. Mostly: a thank-you to Reggie that doubles as a nudge to everyone else.
- **Product (Broccoli):** ✅ **Reggie's actual order confirmed: Kadia + Eliora Leather Handbag — Top Grain Leather Version.** Name BOTH in scene (Kadia received first, Eliora as the matching second handbag — Top Grain version = premium tier, naturally explains his "extremely proud" wife reaction without listicle). 60% OFF MD pricing referenced once, in scene. May 1 order-by date for May 10 arrival = the only "urgency" allowed.
  - ⚠️ Kadia callback opportunity: U-012 Apr 19 Jennifer SOS Q3 mentioned "Kadia Medium sold out — Kadia Small still available." Reggie likely got the Small. Optional one-line nod for repeat readers ("the Kadia some of you read about in Jennifer's SOS — Reggie has one. Top grain version. His wife has it now.").
  - ⚠️ Top Grain emphasis: distinguishes from vegan-leather grievance pattern (G-0419 Gwendolyn "I would never have paid that price 4 a vegan bag when I could of had the real thing"). Naming "Top Grain" once = silent reassurance to that audience without addressing it directly.
- **Character:**
  - **Michelle** — POV, reading the reply, sitting with "the mostest", doing the calendar math
  - **Reggie** — verbatim quote (typos + lowercase + missing apostrophes preserved). DO NOT clean up "i love the mostest." That's the point.
  - **George P.S.** — light: "George read this over my shoulder. He said 'I should write Reggie a letter.' I asked why. He said 'guy solidarity.' He hasn't written it yet. I'm not holding my breath but I'm also not ruling it out."
  - ⚠️ **NO Keisha** (carried Apr 24 Survey — save for Earth Day callback or W18 mid-week)
  - ⚠️ **NO Alice/Marcus/Tasha/Nia** in scene (Reggie's verbatim voice carries the email; team density would dilute him)
- **Law check:**
  - #1 ONE throughline ✓ (men love quietly — sometimes the love letter sneaks out the back of a logistics email — and Mother's Day is closer than you think)
  - #2 Michelle IN scene ✓ (reading reply, sitting with "the mostest", doing May 1/May 10 math out loud)
  - #3 Inhabit ✓ (the reply on screen, the lowercase "i", the wife's face beat, the calendar)
  - #4 Turn ✓ (was going to private-thank-you Reggie → publishes it instead → realizes it doubles as a deadline reminder)
  - #5 Paste raw customer words ✓ (typos + lowercase preserved — DO NOT highlight typos per memory rule)
  - #6 Em dash ≤ 2-3 ✓ (target ≤ 2 across full email)
  - #7 N/A (email)
  - #8 Opening = customer voice + warm hook in 3-5 lines ✓
  - #9 Product stays in scene ✓ (60% OFF + May 1 cutoff woven into Reggie's "two ahead" beat — NOT a separator/listicle)
  - #10 No triple-And ✓
- **Throughline:** Some of the loudest love letters come from people who didn't think they were writing one. Eleven women in Reggie's family are about to find out — and Mother's Day is closer than the calendar feels. Order by May 1 if you want her to hold it on May 10.
- **Subject Line Ideas:**
  - "I love them the mostest."
  - "Reggie signed off and I sat down."
  - "A grandfather wrote me back."
  - "Eleven females. One grandfather."
  - "He didn't think he was writing a love letter."
- **Structure:**
  1. Cold open — the reply lands, the sign-off line, Michelle reading it three times
  2. Backfill (one line) — what email he was replying to (Apr 24 Survey)
  3. **Verbatim quote block** (purse + handbag + wife's face + sign-off — strip USPS paragraph)
  4. The math — 11 women, "the mostest"
  5. "The mostest" beat — that word, why it lands
  6. Turn — was going to thank him privately, publishing it instead
  7. **Pivot to MD-shipping deadline (in scene):** Reggie's second handbag in transit → working through the 11 → "which means he ordered before today" → MD May 10 → 60% OFF MD pricing runs until May 10 → **order by May 1** for guaranteed before-MD arrival
  8. Address reader — if you're a grandfather/daughter/son/husband
  9. Soft close — thank-you to Reggie that doubles as nudge

  11. Optional P.P.S. — one line directly to Reggie ("Reggie if you're reading this — finish the list. We'll keep packing.")

  - DO NOT recap the Survey email (one line max — readers either saw it Apr 24 or they didn't, recap = drag)
  - 60% OFF + May 1 cutoff must land **inside** Reggie's narrative ("his second is in transit → which means he ordered before today → which is the right side of the May 1 line") — NOT as a corporate "P.S. — Mother's Day is coming, here's the deal" block
  - Verify "60% OFF" matches actual ongoing MD pricing on site before send (currently extrapolated from sale's "up to 82% off" — extended pricing likely lower max, ~60% sounds right but confirm with user)
  - Verify May 1 cutoff matches Marcus's actual shipping math (8-9 day standard transit + buffer for May 10 arrival = May 1 hard date is operationally honest)
  - George P.S. tone = warm-light, not slapstick (he's reading over her shoulder = intimate, not comedic prop)

### R-022-archived: "Alice Made Dylan Lock Me Out" — The $19.95 Sabotage + Gate Closes Tonight
- **Theme:** Behind the Scenes + CLOSE (actual gate shut) + JUSTIFY (why some bags ended up $19.95) + Seinfeld Moment
- **Story Source:** Product Origin (founder POV) + Campaign Job (CLOSE) + Team conflict
- **Emotional Driver:** Conspiratorial joy (you're inside the rebellion) + Mother's Day conviction ("worth every cent") + Comic-panic (Alice financial fire)
- **Hook (Hot Dog):** "Alice told Dylan — our IT guy — to block my access to the admin system. And honestly? She's not wrong. I did it again. The plan said $29.95. I made some of them $19.95. Same bags that sit on the site at $109.95 and up. I didn't tell her. She found out. Dylan got the email at 6:47 this morning."
- **Bridge:** Michelle's rebellion-as-love: she "slipped" somewhere between the plan and the save button. Doesn't name which bags (keeps the $19.95 a surprise for Tuesday — registered Queens only). Alice's financial panic lands as a one-line fire (callback to C-012 pattern). Dylan arrives as a NEW cast member: the IT guy who follows orders, doesn't fight Michelle — just flips the switch. Turn: Michelle tries to log in mid-morning, gets the "permission denied" screen, doesn't even fight it. Sits back. Thinks about the faces. "Mother's Day will blossom with the looks on their faces as they open their gifts. That's what I kept thinking. That's why I didn't just leave it at $29.95." Cap beat lands inside the scene, not tacked on: "~100 of you left before we hit 5,000. Gate closes tonight. Not Monday. Not 'soon.' Tonight." BOGO sidebar (one short paragraph, not a section): "A lot of you are writing in asking me to bring the matching-wallet-free offer back. I'm not. This one is better. Dylan would agree if he could log me back in long enough to show you."
- **Product (Broccoli):** The $19.95 sabotage tier — DO NOT name the specific bags. Name the pattern: "Same bags that retail $109.95+. Same Keisha standard. A price I wasn't supposed to publish. A price Alice didn't approve. A price only the 5,000 registered will actually see Tuesday morning." Optional callback to First Four (U-011) — "those four names you saw Saturday? They're in the pile. So are some I haven't named yet."
- **Character:** Michelle (POV — rebellion + conviction), Alice (financial fire — one-line panic, then the Dylan move — comedic + velvet-rope credibility), **Dylan (NEW — IT guy, S-049a character)** — silent enforcer, signs emails "Admin access revoked per A. Request. — D.", never speaks in scene. George asleep. Keisha/Marcus/Tasha OFF for cast-density (Jennifer + Cassandra carried Apr 19; today is Michelle-Alice-Dylan-only).
- **Law:** #1 ONE throughline · #2 Michelle IN scene (permission-denied screen, 6:47 AM email, the save button memory) · #3 Inhabit (the screen, the email timestamp, the $19.95 vs $29.95 vs $109.95 price ladder) · #4 Turn (Michelle tries to log in → locked out → sits back → thinks about faces) · #9 Product stays in scene (price ladder woven, not listicled) · #10 No triple-And anaphora
- **Throughline:** Some rules are worth breaking. My accountant doesn't agree. My IT guy has orders. Mother's Day is tonight at midnight — or whenever 100 more of you text MOM — whichever first.
- **Layer revealed (Apr 20 CLOSE):** Actual gate-close time/trigger (TODAY, not "soon") + $19.95 anchor as proof "registered only" isn't marketing — it's literal price quarantine + Alice/Dylan as enforcement mechanism = velvet rope is a real door, not a metaphor + BOGO closure (acknowledges the question without reopening)
- **Subject Line Ideas:**
  - "Alice made Dylan block me."
  - "I got locked out of my own admin."
  - "The price Alice didn't approve."
  - "$19.95. Alice is going to kill me."
  - "Dylan flipped the switch. I don't blame him."
  - "I did it again. (Alice found out.)"
- **Structure:**
  1. Cold open (Alice → Dylan → the 6:47 AM email → permission-denied screen)
  2. Confession ($19.95 vs $29.95 vs $109.95 — the slip)
  3. Alice's fire (one-line panic → callback to "you did it AGAIN" energy from C-012)
  4. Turn (Michelle tries to log in → locked out → doesn't fight → sits back)
  5. The WHY ("Mother's Day will blossom with the looks on their faces...")
  6. Gate reality (~100 spots to 5K, closes tonight)
  7. BOGO sidebar (one short paragraph — no, we're not bringing it back, this is better)
  8. CTA (Text MOM → 94923 → before Dylan locks the registration page too)
  9. P.S. (one line — George / Nia wisdom / or Dylan signing off)
- **Campaign Fit:** Apr 20 CLOSE slot. Replaces W17 planned PREPARE (Marcus pulled stacks). Gate is still open → this is the ACTUAL close, not Apr 19's vague FAQ close. Works because: (a) introduces deal hype ($19.95) without revealing which bags, (b) uses team conflict as velvet-rope credibility (Dylan's block = proof prices are real), (c) closes the gate with specific math (~100 left) + time (tonight), (d) addresses BOGO question that's been clogging customer-voices without reopening the offer.
- **Stakes/CTA mechanic:** Text MOM → 94923 → claim one of the last ~100 spots before 5K cap OR tonight's close, whichever first. Registered = see the $19.95 Tuesday morning. Not registered = see $29.95 OR nothing (if cap holds).
- **Hits Teaser 3-element checklist (memory rule):**
  - ✅ Private mechanic: "Alice made Dylan lock me out of my own admin" = velvet-rope as literal door
  - ✅ Demand signal: ~100 spots before 5K cap, gate closes tonight
  - ✅ Prices: $19.95 reveal (vs $29.95 planned, vs $109.95+ retail) — woven in scene, not corporate block
- **⚠️ Watchouts:**
  - Don't name which bags are at $19.95. Tease the tier, don't reveal the list. (List reveal = Apr 21 LIVE email.)
  - Dylan is NEW. Keep him silent (emails only, no dialogue in scene). Sign-off device: "— D." Adds to universe; doesn't hijack it.
  - BOGO sidebar must be ONE short paragraph, not a section. If it grows = it hijacks the CLOSE job.
  - Alice capped at 1 scene-beat (already at 3 W17 days — Apr 19 off, Apr 20 on as the spark, Apr 22 Earth Day OFF to preserve density rule).
  - Don't over-explain "worth every cent" — let the faces-opening-gifts line carry it. One beat.
- **Source:** User direction 2026-04-20 (price-sabotage + Dylan block + BOGO question + Mother's Day conviction) + extends C-012 "Alice caught me lowering prices again" pattern + S-049 BOGO-question cluster
- **Added:** 2026-04-20
- **🔒 PRIMARY CANDIDATE for Apr 20 CLOSE slot.** Pairs with SMS MASS teaser (see below — R-022-SMS draft).

### R-016: "Marcus Wrote 1000 On The Whiteboard" — The Mother's Day Delivery Cap
- **Theme:** Behind the Scenes + JUSTIFY (cap reveal) + Operational Promise
- **Story Source:** Product Origin / Warehouse scene + Campaign Job (cap announcement)
- **Emotional Driver:** Conspiratorial trust (you're being shown the math) + Customer-protective scarcity
- **Hook (Hot Dog):** "Marcus walked into my office. He didn't say a word. He held up a calendar. Pointed to May 10. Then Apr 23. Then he walked to my whiteboard, picked up the marker, and wrote one number. **1000.** Then he tapped the marker on the board twice. Like he was finishing a sentence I hadn't said out loud yet."
- **Bridge:** Michelle does the math out loud so the reader does it with her. MD = May 10. Sale closes Apr 23. That's 17 days for the warehouse to pull, pack, ship, and LAND every bag in a mother's hand before MD morning. 4 packers. Average 60 bags/packer/day at this care level. Marcus did the multiplication. **1000 is the absolute ceiling that lets him promise every gift arrives BEFORE May 10.** Order 1001? Somebody's mom unwraps wrapping paper on May 11. Marcus won't allow it. So he capped it. Pivot: "I told Marcus we could probably squeeze in 1100. He looked at me like I'd just asked him to lie to a grandmother." → Reveal: that's why this isn't a 'while supplies last' sale. It's a 'while the calendar holds' sale. → Callback to The 300 Mission: "Six weeks ago we capped at 300 because the cause demanded it. This time we cap at 1000 because YOUR MOTHER demands it. Different number. Same kind of line."
- **Product (Broccoli):** The full MD lineup (Wallets, Circle Crossbody, Imani, Heritage Tote, Barakaya, Baldisa) — the cap applies to TOTAL orders, not per-bag. Mention 2-3 bestsellers by name without listicle.
- **Character:** Marcus (S-028 angle — "the man who communicates in nods" — silent, calendar, marker, whiteboard), Michelle (POV + math out loud), brief Alice nod ("Alice walked past, saw the 1000, and for the first time in three months didn't say anything about my margins. She just nodded.")
- **Law:** #1 ONE throughline · #2 Michelle IN scene · #3 Inhabit (calendar, marker, whiteboard, the silent tap-tap) · #4 Every scene has a turn (Michelle pushes for 1100 → Marcus's grandmother look) · #9 Product stays in scene
- **Throughline:** This cap isn't marketing scarcity. It's the maximum number of mothers we can promise will hold their gift before May 10.
- **Layer revealed (W16 teaser arc):** The cap (1000) + the WHY (delivery math, not stock) + Marcus as enforcement + callback to 300 Mission credibility
- **Subject Line Ideas:**
  - "Marcus wrote a number on my whiteboard."
  - "1000. That's the line."
  - "The reason the sale closes at 1000."
  - "Marcus did the math. Then he capped it."
- **Structure:** Cold open (Marcus walks in silent) → The number on the board → Michelle does the math out loud (calendar dates, packer capacity) → Turn (Michelle pushes 1100, Marcus's look) → Pivot to product lineup in scene (Marcus walks her past the pulled stacks) → 300 Mission callback → CTA (Text MOM, 1000 spots, when it closes the calendar closes it)
- **Campaign Fit:** Apr 17 PROVE/Customer Voice slot REPLACEMENT. Reframes Friday from customer-proof to **structural proof** — the cap proves the deal is real, the deadline proves the cap is real. Sets up Sat-Sun emails (#7-#9) to reference "spots remaining" with credibility.
- **Stakes/CTA mechanic:** Register → claim one of the 1000 → Marcus closes the door when it fills OR when calendar runs out, whichever first. Same MOM → 94923 mechanic from W16 sequence. Reader's registration becomes a literal seat at the table.
- **Source:** User direction 2026-04-17 (1000 cap brief) + S-028 Marcus rare-speech angle + The 300 Mission precedent (`examples/iwd-300-mission/`)
- **Added:** 2026-04-17

### R-017: "Keisha Said 1000. Then She Said Why." — The QC Cap

So we don't sell 1001. → Optional Bald & Bougie callback (Apr 14 U-008): "You remember the photo on her desk. The one she framed. THAT is the standard. 1000 bags get that standard. So 1000 is the line."

### R-021-archived: "I Leaked It To My Favs Last Night. Here Are The Four." — The Forward-It Lineup Reveal
- **Theme:** Behind the Scenes + JUSTIFY/TEACH hybrid + Product Reveal With Prices
- **Story Source:** Product Origin (last-touch CEO scene) + Customer Voice (SMS reactions from HIGH leak)

- **Hook (Hot Dog):** "I sat down last night to FINISH the Mother's Day lineup. Confirm prices. Hit save. Close laptop. Bed. Instead I screenshotted four of them, opened my texts, and sent it to my favorite customers with the line *don't screenshot this lol.* Tasha read the SMS over my shoulder this morning. She said, 'Michelle. They're going to forward it anyway.' I said good. So this morning I'm forwarding it myself."
- **Bridge:** Michelle leaks the SAME four she texted HIGH on Apr 16 — but reframes each by the NAME, not the price. The names are Swahili and English wordplay (Fahari = "pride", Barakaya = "blessed", Imarimom = acrostic spine, Godfidence = "God + confidence"). The frame: you're not buying a wallet or a handbag — you're buying a WORD she'll carry. Pivot to cap reality (3,573 registered, 1,000 spots, 4 days). Closer: "If you got the SMS Wednesday, you saw this already. If you didn't — now you have. Same prices. Same line. Same MOM to 94923."
  1. **Fahari Wallet** ($49.95 → **$9.95**) — Swahili for "pride." For the mother who never let you see her struggle.
  2. **Barakaya Wallet** ($49.95 → **$9.95**) — "Just Blessed." For the mother who answers "how are you?" with "blessed and highly favored" — and means it every time. *(Callback: U-009 Nia's piggy bank pick. Camesha cried at her desk over this one — R-015.)*
  3. **Imarimom Small Leather Handbag** ($131.95 → **From $29.95**) — Read the spine down the side: SMART · STRONG · BEAUTIFUL · THOUGHTFUL · PATIENT · SUPER · WOMAN. For the mother you couldn't summarize in one word, so Keisha used seven.
  4. **Godfidence Small Leather Handbag** ($131.95 → **From $29.95**) — "She Who Kneels Before God Can Stand Before Anyone." For the mother who faced the principal, the doctor, the funeral director — and never lost her voice.

  - "Fahari. Barakaya. Imarimom. Godfidence."
- **Structure:** Cold open (Michelle late, finish-the-lineup intent → text screenshot instead) → Tasha-this-morning beat (over-shoulder, "they'll forward it anyway") → "So I'm forwarding it myself" pivot → 4 products in scene, name + frame + price (one short paragraph each, not bullets) → Cap reality (3,573/1,000, 4 days) → CTA (MOM → 94923) → P.S. (1 line — Alice/George/Marcus pick one, keep it light)

R-021 better if Sat needs deal credibility (real prices visible) + cap urgency in one beat + cross-channel proof (HIGH saw it, MASS sees it now). R-020 better if Sat should stay story-led without revealing specific prices.

### R-020: "Deborah Is 68. She Has A Michelle Obama Bag. She Wants One From Me."

The lesson is: your money, your choice, learn to spend it. Pivot: "There's a private sale Tuesday. Early Mother's Day. If you're going to spend your money, spend it smart. Register. Wait three days." → Nia opens the laptop, scrolls, stops on the Barakaya Wallet. "This one. It says 'Just Blessed.'" Michelle goes quiet. Because those are the two words she'd tell every subscriber every morning if she could. Her 10-year-old just picked THE wallet. With her own money. For her grandma. Closing beat: if this deal is good enough for Michelle's own daughter to wait three days and register — it's real. Text MOM.

- **Character:** Nia (main — giver moment, wise-beyond-years), Michelle (witness + teacher + emotional anchor). Grandma = Nia's grandma (user to confirm: maternal = Michelle's mom, or paternal = George's mom). Both are canonical-available — no "gone mom" premise. George/Alice NOT in scene.
- **Law:** #1 ONE throughline · #2 Michelle IN scene · #3 Inhabit (piggy bank, laptop, scroll stop) · #4 Every scene has a turn (almost gives her one → stops → teaches instead) · #9 Product stays in scene
- **Throughline:** Even the giver has to learn to give smart — and a 10-year-old with her own money picked the wallet that says what I'd say every morning.

### R-013-archived: "The Photo on Keisha's Desk" — Bald & Bougie + Canvas Promise
- **Theme:** Behind the Scenes + Customer Spotlight + Product Story (representation)
- **Story Source:** Customer Voice + Product Origin + BTS workshop moment
- **Emotional Driver:** Pride + Belonging (seeing yourself) + Team tenderness
- **Hook (Hot Dog):** "I walked into Keisha's studio this morning to pick bags for the Early Mother's Day Sale. I was supposed to be working. Instead I stopped. There was a photo on her desk I'd never seen before. Framed. Wooden frame. Sitting right next to the leather rolls and the thread spools."
- **Bridge:** The scene unfolds in order:
  1. Michelle sees the framed photo on Keisha's workbench (leather rolls in background, sewing machine, thread spools, the frame propped up like it belongs there). A woman in a colorful print dress, shaved head, holding a Baldisa in a hallway. Michelle has to photograph it immediately to show everyone today.
  2. Asks Keisha: "Who is she?" Keisha: "Jennifer from Support sent it to me. It's a review off our site. Queen named Bald & Bougie. Lol. I don't know her real name."
  3. Keisha reads the review aloud (or Michelle reads it aloud, verbatim, typos-and-emoji intact):
     > "I LOVE IT! Making the decision to shave my head included wanting to FULLY embrace it. As soon as I saw this and the Baridi design I knew I had to have them. They stepped up my accessory game and now are staple pieces 😍"
  4. Quiet beat. Michelle realizes Keisha FRAMED IT. Not pinned. Not saved to phone. FRAMED. Like it was already art.
  5. Michelle's promise, out loud, in the moment: "If we hit 5,000 registrations for Early Mother's Day Sale, I'm printing this at 100cm and hanging it on the wall behind you. Canvas. Real frame."
  6. Current count: 1,000+. Need 4,000 more. 7 days to go.
  7. Reveal: The Baldisa — the EXACT bag in Bald & Bougie's hallway — is in the Early MD Sale at **$29.95** (normally $131.95).
- **Product (Broccoli):** Baldisa Leather Handbag — $29.95 sale price (was $131.95). Baridi design as secondary mention.
- **Character:** Michelle (catches the moment, makes the promise), Keisha (quiet designer who framed a stranger's review), Jennifer from Support Team (off-screen — the one who saw it first and sent it)
- **Law:** #1 Personality + #15 Intimate Details (the frame, the leather rolls, the 😍 emoji) + #4 Social Proof (1,000+ registered, stranger framed on desk)
- **Throughline:** Some reviews you read. Some reviews you frame.
- **Subject Line Ideas:**
  - "There was a photo on Keisha's desk."
  - "Keisha framed a stranger."
  - "I made Keisha a promise this morning."
  - "Who is Bald & Bougie?"
- **Structure:**
  1. Cold open — Michelle walks into Keisha's studio (the workshop scene details)
  2. Discovery — the framed photo, the propping, the "wait what"
  3. Dialogue — "Who is she?" / "Jennifer sent it. Queen named Bald & Bougie. Lol."
  4. The review (verbatim, typos/emoji intact)
  5. The quiet beat — "she FRAMED it"
  6. The promise — 5,000 registrations = 100cm canvas, hung behind Keisha's seat
  7. The count — "We're at 1,000+. I need 4,000 more Queens. 7 days."
  8. Pivot — "Oh. And that bag? The one in Bald & Bougie's hallway? Baldisa. $29.95 in the sale. Was $131.95."
  9. CTA — Text MOM to register (help Michelle keep her promise to Keisha)
  10. P.S. — Keisha beat (designer's "I knew" voice) OR Jennifer beat (thank-you to Support Team)
- **Campaign Fit:** Apr 14 PROVE day — registration count climbing + customer proof + BTS scene all in one story. Sale-teaser layer = Baldisa price reveal ($131.95 → $29.95 = 77% off framing).
- **Stakes/CTA mechanic:** Register → help hit 5K → Keisha gets her canvas. Makes the reader's registration ACTIVE, not passive. Queen becomes part of team story.
- **Pull-from-real-quote rule:** Use the review EXACTLY as written. Don't clean up "😍" or "LOL" or caps on "FULLY." The whole point is that Keisha framed it raw.
- **Source:** TrustPilot/website review — "Bald & Bougie" (Apr 11, 2026), photo attached, forwarded by Jennifer from Support

### R-031-archived: "Marcus and USPS Are Talking. Here's What You Actually Need." — May 1 Shipping-Tier Honesty
- **Theme:** Industry Commentary + Behind the Scenes (Marcus callback) + structural deadline honesty
- **Story Source:** Industry Commentary (USPS + FedEx published May 1 cutoff) + Product Origin (Marcus warehouse / shipping math)
- **Emotional Driver:** Vulnerability (Michelle has been over-warning) → Conspiratorial trust (Marcus correcting the founder = real ops transparency) → Honest urgency without panic
- **Campaign Job:** None — Daily (W18 Friday, post-Bonnie female rebalance + MD W19 setup)
- **Hook (Hot Dog):**
  > I read a news article this morning. USPS just published their Mother's Day shipping deadlines. The First Class cutoff: today. May 1. FedEx Home Delivery: also today.
  >
  > I walked over to Marcus. Showed him the article. He didn't even look up.
  >
  > He said: *"Michelle. It's not that simple."*
- **Bridge (6-beat, in scene):**
  1. **Marcus correction (the turn):** *"I told you that two weeks ago — but I also told you we have THREE shipping tiers. You keep telling people 'order by May 1' like it's a wall. It's not a wall. It's a fork."*
  2. **The fork explained (in scene — Marcus on the whiteboard, REAL numbers):**
     - **Economy** ⚠️ — *"Lands May 9 to May 12. That's the cheap one. May 10 is in there. So is May 12. I can't promise which day. If she opens it on May 11, that's on the carrier. Not on us."*
     - **Standard** ✅ — *"Lands May 6 to May 9. Saturday at the latest. That's the lane I'd pick if I were you."*
     - **Express** 🚀 — *"Lands May 4 to May 5. She has it next weekend. You watch her open it before MD even hits."*
  3. **Michelle's confession:** *"I've been writing 'order by May 1' in every email like Economy was the safe lane. Marcus just told me I had it backwards. May 1 is when Economy STOPS being safe. Standard is the safe lane now. I've been pointing people at the cheap option like it was a guarantee. It isn't. Not anymore."*
  4. **The honest reframe:** *"Here's the actual math. Economy saves you money but might land May 11 or 12. Standard lands by Saturday May 9 — one day before. Express lands next weekend, you give it before MD even shows up. There isn't a wrong answer. There's a lane that fits how much risk you want to take with your mother's face on Sunday morning."*
  5. **Customer cameo (Terray, light):** *"Terray didn't wait for any deadline. Gave hers to her mom Tuesday. Sent us the video. The deadline doesn't matter when you've already done it."*
  6. **Soft CTA in scene:** Order today for Economy savings, or pick the tier that fits your timeline. 60% off MD2026 still on. May 10 is still May 10.
- **Product (Broccoli):** Open lineup, 60% off MD2026. The shipping tier choice IS the urgency, not "deal ends." Optional Aina Coconut White callback (U-018 continuity) OR keep generic "the bag for your mom."
- **Character:**
  - **Michelle** (POV — reads news, walks to Marcus, gets corrected, confesses to readers)
  - **Marcus** (silent enforcer canon broken — speaks 2-3 lines for the correction; whiteboard reappears as the structural device, callback to R-016 Apr 17)
  - **Terray** (1-line cameo + "video she sent us" reference — anti-pressure-release counterpoint)
  - ⚠️ NO George/Alice/Keisha/Tasha — keep cast tight, Marcus carries this one
  - ⚠️ Marcus usage: last seen R-016 Apr 17 (whiteboard 1000 cap). Two-week gap honors his rare-speech canon. He's correcting Michelle here = breaks "silent" pattern but earns it through structural honesty.
- **Law check:**
  - #1 ONE throughline ✓ (the deadline isn't a wall, it's a fork)
  - #2 Michelle IN scene ✓ (reads article, walks to Marcus, gets corrected)
  - #3 Inhabit ✓ (article on phone, Marcus's office, the whiteboard, the 3 tiers written down)
  - #4 Turn ✓ (Michelle's "USPS confirms my deadline" → Marcus's "you've been scaring people")
  - #5 Don't pre-sell ✓ (jump-cut into article + Marcus correction)
  - #6 Standalone ✓ (R-016 Marcus callback works without prior read — whiteboard device explained in scene)
  - #17 Em dash ≤ 2-3 ✓ (target)
  - #22 Product in scene ✓ (no listicle — shipping tiers ARE the product structure today)
  - #26 No naked pivot ✓ (CTA enters via Marcus's whiteboard, not corporate block)
  - #28 No echo writing ✓ (vary tier descriptions — don't parallel-structure all 3)
- **Throughline:** *"Economy used to be the safe lane. Today it stopped. Standard is the new floor. Express buys you a weekend reveal. Pick the risk you can live with."*
- **Subject Line Ideas:**
  - "Marcus just corrected me."
  - "I had Economy backwards."
  - "May 1 is when Economy stops being safe."
  - "Standard is the new floor."
  - "There's three lanes. I picked the wrong one to point at."
  - "I've been telling you the wrong thing."
- **Preview Line Ideas:**
  - "Economy might land May 11. That's after Mother's Day."
  - "Standard by Saturday. Express by next weekend. Pick your risk."
  - "Marcus walked me to the whiteboard. I had it backwards."
- **Structure:**
  1. Cold open — news article + walk to Marcus + Marcus's "it's not that simple"
  2. Marcus correction — "you've been telling people the wrong thing"
  3. Whiteboard scene — 3 tiers explained (Economy / Standard / Express) with deadlines
  4. Michelle's confession — "I've been scaring people"
  5. Honest reframe — pick the lane that fits your life
  6. Terray cameo (1-2 lines) — the anti-deadline release
  7. Soft CTA + button — order today (Economy) or later (Standard/Express)
  8. Close — "May 10 is still May 10"
  9. P.S. — light Marcus or Terray nod (TBD)
- **Target length:** ~450-550 words. Honest-correction email = needs the whiteboard scene to land + 3-tier breakdown legible. NOT essay-length.
- **Campaign Fit:** May 1 W18 Friday daily — Industry Commentary primary (USPS news cycle) + Behind the Scenes (Marcus correction). Female-leaning cast (Michelle solo + silent-broken Marcus + Terray) rebalances after Apr 26-29 male-thematic compounding. Bridges from R-027 Bonnie Apr 30 (TX→NJ choreography, "carrier window closes Friday") → R-031 May 1 (USPS confirms it, Marcus refines it).
- **⚠️ Risks / Watchouts:**
  - 🟢 **Shipping tier numbers VERIFIED 2026-05-01 from Afroyla checkout screenshot:** Economy May 09-12 / Standard May 06-09 / Express May 04-05. These are LIVE checkout estimates as of May 1 — re-verify just before send if the email goes out late in the day.
  - 🔴 **Honest framing flip:** Economy on May 1 is NO LONGER the safe lane (May 11/12 = post-MD risk). Standard ($) is the new floor. Email must land this honestly — don't soften "Economy might land May 11" into "Economy still works." It might not. That's the whole point of Marcus's correction.
  - 🔴 **Don't make Express sound like the "premium upsell"** — frame it as "watch her open it next weekend, before MD even shows up." Gift-now energy, not panic-buy energy. Marcus is correcting Michelle's pressure tactics, not adding new ones.
  - 🟡 **Marcus speaks here** — breaks his "silent enforcer" canon (R-016, R-018, U-013-archived). Earned via the structural-honesty turn (he's correcting his boss = vulnerability beat). But cap him at 3-4 lines max — don't expand him into a full sitcom partner.
  - 🟡 **Terray cameo** — must be ≤ 2 lines + the video reference. Don't quote her email (the moment is small). Verify Terray's video is usable as UGC OR just reference "she sent us a video" without showing.
  - 🟡 **Avoid contradicting prior "May 1" emails** — Apr 26 Reggie, Apr 27 Career, Apr 29 Aina FAQ all said "order by May 1." This email REFRAMES that as "May 1 = Economy tier deadline, not the only deadline." The confession beat handles it: "I've been writing it in every email." Acknowledge, don't gaslight.
  - 🟡 **Apr 30 Bonnie** sets up the carrier-window urgency — May 1 R-031 LANDS the structural correction. Sequencing: Bonnie = "carrier window closes Friday" (urgent), R-031 = "yes, but Marcus says there's 3 windows" (honest). Don't undercut Bonnie — REFINE her.
  - 🟢 **News cycle alignment** — USPS + FedEx published deadlines today. Search-result-aligned email = high opens. Subject line "Marcus just corrected me" works against the news framing.
- **Hits Industry Commentary 3-element checklist:**
  - ✅ External hook (USPS + FedEx published cutoff = phenomenon)
  - ✅ Internal correction (Marcus corrects Michelle = vulnerability)
  - ✅ Audience action (3-tier choice, not panic-buy)

### R-034-archived: "Caralen Is Waiting For The Right Time." — Just Blessed + Commit To Your Priority Order
- **Theme:** Customer Voice + Michelle's World (priority-honoring) + soft Express Shipping nudge
- **Story Source:** Customer Voice (S-0501a Caralen Deaconess Temoney) + Brand-values reframe
- **Emotional Driver:** Honor (her priority order) → Permission (waiting IS commitment, not failing) → Decisive joy (Just Blessed = name your moment, then live it)
- **Campaign Job:** None — Daily (W18 Saturday May 02)
- **Hook (Hot Dog):**
  > "Caralen wrote me yesterday. She owns one of our bags. She loves it. She wants another. She can't afford it right now.
  >
  > She didn't write to ask for a discount. She wrote to tell me where she is."
- **Bridge (5-beat, in scene):**
  1. **Caralen verbatim block (Rule #8 — preserve voice intact, do NOT highlight any typos):** Her own words about caring for her mom through lung cancer treatments, her own anxiety and depression, working at church for no pay because *"what I do I do for God, not for money or a pat on the back."* The Deaconess identity. The signature: *"Character is key because that's who you are when nobody's watching you."* Close with her sentence: *"I would really love another bag, I have 1 and I love it, I was working then. This is who I am."*
  2. **Michelle's reaction (sit-down beat):** "I read this email twice. Sat with it. Then I read it again. Caralen is not asking me for anything. She's telling me where she is. **And she's telling me she's coming back.**" Body action — Michelle puts the phone down, looks at the calendar, doesn't pivot to product yet.
  3. **The reframe — priority order as commitment, not deferral:** "Cuộc sống là vậy. Mỗi thời điểm chúng ta sẽ có thứ tự ưu tiên khác nhau. Right now, Caralen's priority order is: her mom's treatments → her own health → her church → herself. **That's not waiting. That's commitment.** The bag isn't off her list. It's just not at the top of her list. *Yet.* And the woman who's clear about her priority order is the woman who eventually gets everything on it." Translate to English in voice — Vietnamese is for me, not the email.
  4. **Just Blessed — name the moment:** Bring in **Barakaya** ("Just Blessed") — not as the bag Caralen ordered (she didn't), but as the bag whose NAME is the philosophy. *Just Blessed.* Two words. The Deaconess sign-off in product form. "When Caralen's moment comes — and it will — Barakaya will be there. Or one of the others. The bag is patient. It's the woman who's clear."
  5. **Soft pivot — Express Shipping for the OTHER reader (the one whose priority IS today):** "Anyway. If you're reading this and your priority THIS week is getting a Mother's Day gift into someone's hands before May 10 — Express Shipping (lands May 4-5) is the lane. Standard (lands May 6-9) is the safe one. Economy (lands May 9-12) is the gamble. Marcus and I had this conversation yesterday. He said pick the lane that fits the risk you can live with. Same logic as Caralen. Name your priority. Honor it."

Lellia's still watching. Sharon's still watching. The village is still watching."
